B00EW9GQR6|5.0|In the words of Tony Bennett, this lady is \\"America's Picasso.\\"<br /><br />Lady Gaga's fourth studio album, ARTPOP, is nothing short of excellence. It isn't quite like The Fame, The Fame Monster, or Born This Way and that's what so impressive and admirable about Gaga - she is constantly changing and evolving musically and artistically. Both lyrically and sonically, the album is fun, catchy, upbeat, but also very intelligent with what it's saying. Though on the surface it doesn't seem nearly as deep and philosophical as Born This Way, it's certainly still filled with meaning and does not lack Gaga's unique metaphors and references to Greek mythology, literature, and works of art (both Renaissance as well as contemporary).<br /><br />ARTPOP is easily the best album of 2013. But...is it better than Born This Way, Gaga's previous record-breaking album? Hmm, that honestly depends on who you ask. Commercially, I believe the general public (people who AREN'T hardcore Gaga fans) and music critics will probably prefer ARTPOP over Born This Way due to its seemingly carefree and fun nature, as Born This Way received a lot of criticism back in 2011 for being \\"too mature\\" because people could not grasp why a pop album had to be so profound and weren't too happy with Gaga touching on the issues of gay rights, illegal immigration, freedom of religion, gender equality, government corruption, etc. on Born This Way. People who weren't too thrilled with that will without doubt enjoy ARTPOP more. However, it was precisely due to those very reasons why Born This Way why such a pop masterpiece and will be hard for Gaga to surpass artistically. If you're looking for a Born This Way 2.0 you will be disappointed because, comparatively, ARTPOP is far more sexual and provocative in the lyrics and less preachy and melancholic. In either case, it's too early to tell if ARTPOP will be better received than Born This Way. But one thing's for sure: it certainly will not disappoint.<br /><br />Now, because one obviously buys an album for its songs, I'm going to a review each song individually below. Here is a track by track review of the album. As with all of her albums, Lady Gaga wrote every single song herself.<br /><br />Quick review of the songs:<br /><br />1. Aura - artistic rebirth and evolution, the opening lyrics states \\"I killed my former\\" which implies the Lady Gaga we came to know from the Born This Way era is dead. The Gaga you will hear on this album is a different Gaga. Also has some feminist lyrics and mention of a metaphorical burqa, a metaphor for Gaga's costumes and stage presence. Do you wanna see the girl who lives behind the burqa? = Do you wanna see the person underneath all the wigs and make-up?<br /><br />2. Venus - artistic rebirth and evolution, a continuation (conceptually-speaking) of the first song. Here, new Gaga is being introduced to us (Birth of Venus).<br /><br />3. G.U.Y. - gender roles and feminism. Gaga implies that women are the dominant ones during sex precisely because they choose to bottom.<br /><br />4. Sexxx Dreams - sexual oppression, the encounter mentioned in the song can only take place in a dream because in the real world it would be frowned upon. References to the novel 1984 by George Orwell.<br /><br />5. Jewels N' Drugs - drug use from a possibly satirical take. Shows Gaga's musically diversity. She did a lot of jazz and rock n roll during Born This Way, and is exploring rap and hip hop here in ARTPOP.<br /><br />6. MANiCURE - love and relationships, the girl in the song seemingly wants to be \\"manicured\\" but really wants to be \\"man-cured\\" (cured from falling in love with men).<br /><br />7. Do What U Want - fame and celebrity culture, Gaga and R. Kelly tell the haters and the critics that they don't deserve an artist's heart and mind so they might as well do whatever they want with the artist's body.<br /><br />8. ARTPOP - art sings to pop in the first verse of the song (\\"come to me, with all your glamour andcruelty\\" - addressing the sexualization of female pop stars) and pop sings to art in the second verse (\\"come to me, with all your subtext and fantasy [...] in a perverse hue\\" - addressing the general public's misunderstanding and lack of appreciation for contemporary art. Thematically, the reverse of Andy Warhol's pop art movement. Genius track.<br /><br />9. Swine - rape and sexual trauma being coped with via a seemingly innocent and upbeat EDM song (don't let the fun beat overpower the dark, dark lyrics! take a look at what she's saying in the song!)<br /><br />10. Donatella - arguably talks about a shallow and vane love for the fashion industry, loving fashion because it makes you feel fabulous. Also seems to talk about men's fear of a strong, confident women.<br /><br />11. Fashion! - undeniably talks about a pure and good-intentioned love for the fashion industry, loving fashion for the beauty and art of it.<br /><br />12. Mary Jane Holland - a positive take on drug use.<br /><br />13. Dope - a negative take of drug use, essentially the complete opposite of the previous song.<br /><br />14. Gypsy - the difficulties of finding love when traveling the world.<br /><br />15. Applause - an ode to theatre and the art of performing. Also a thank you to fanbases.<br /><br />More detailed review and analysis for those interested:<br /><br />1. Aura<br /><br />Lady Gaga stated multiple times in interviews that the order of the songs on ARTPOP mattered, as they're intended to be listened in a certain order for the sake of continuity and abstract storytelling. This certainly proves true as the opening line of Aura, the very first track on the CD, states \\"I killed my former and left her in the truck on Highway 10 / Put the knife under the hood, if you find it send it straight to Hollywood.\\" That opening line is very important for understanding what the song is about and actually what the album as a whole is going to be about. Gaga is letting us know that she \\"killed her former\\" - meaning that she's left behind the Gaga we heard on Born This Way and that the Gaga on ARTPOP is going to be a different Gaga. Lyrically, the rest of the song talks about wanting to meet the mysterious girl who lives behind a metaphorical burqa. The chorus goes, \\"Do you wanna see me naked, lover? Do you wanna peek underneath the covers? Do you wanna see the girl who lives behind the aura?\\" While intentionally provocative, there's more to those lyrics than just their sexual implications. Gaga is asking you, the listener, if you want to see the real her - the woman behind the mask and theatrical costumes. The woman behind that aura of unapproachability and mystique that seems to fascinate so many. She's essentially asking you if you want to see the human being behind the Lady Gaga character, and that's an awesome way to start off the album. Additionally, the bridge introduces us to the various themes and topics that will be explored on the album (\\"Dance, sex, art, pop, tech\\") so it's really no surprise why Gaga placed this song as the album opener. Sonically, the song starts off acoustically with vocals reminiscent to those in \\"Judas\\" and a killer guitar, then gets very electronic and techno. It's probably one of my favorite tracks on the whole CD. Very, very catchy. My favorite lyric is, \\"Enigma popstar is fun, she wears burqa for fashion. It's not a statement as much as just a move of passion.\\"<br /><br />2. Venus<br /><br />Prior to the album's release, Lady Gaga made numerous public appearance dressed as Venus, the Greek goddess of love, as depicted by Botticelli in his famous painting \\"Birth of Venus.\\" Because in the previous track, Aura, we learned that Gaga killed her former, we now understand that she is about to be reborn as Venus during this song (literally, it's the birth of Venus). It's interesting to note how much Gaga has played with the concept of rebirth throughout her albums, as it was a theme she explored in both The Fame Monster and Born ThisWay as well. Lyrically, the song talk about taking a journey through space on a rocket and both the Greek goddess Venus as well as the planet Venus are mentioned. Metaphorically, it becomes quite obvious as the song progresses that Gaga is asking us to take a journey with her through the album, as the \\"outer space\\" talked about in the song seems to be alluding the album itself and the \\"planets\\" mentioned at the end is most likely a metaphor for the rest of the songs on the CD. But again, even ignoring this, the song is a fun pop song nonetheless. Sonically, it's a very fun song to dance to that seems to borrow an 80's dance-pop sound that you might hear a gay night club, and the chorus is INCREDIBLY CATCHY. Another favorite of mine.<br /><br />3. G.U.Y. (Girl Under You)<br /><br />G.U.Y. is, without question, one of the more provocative songs on the album! G.U.Y. starts off where Venus left off (conceptually speaking) and begins with a spoken introduction by Himeros, god of sexual desire, who proceeds to tell us that the song will serve as a how-to guide on new sexual positions in the  bedroom. The technical diction and seriousness of the intro makes the song comical right from the start, and the addictive chorus (probably the catchiest chorus in the whole album, but that's just my opinion) makes the song a memorable one and arguably the best one on the whole album. The song is lyrically very feminist as Gaga sings about how women are in fact the dominant ones in bed precisely because they usually act as the submissive partner. In other words, the \\"bottom.\\" Gaga tells the man in the song that if it wasn't for the G.U.Y. (the Girl Under You), the man who is topping wouldn't have anyone to please or anyone to please him. Undeniably a very interesting point to raise about sex! My favorite line comes from the end of the song, \\"Touch me, touch me, don't be shy, I'm in charge like a G.U.Y. I'll lay down, face up this time, under you like a G.U.Y. I wanna be that G.U.Y.! The girl under you, guy!\\"<br /><br />4. Sexxx Dreams<br /><br />After the how-to guide provided by the lyrics in G.U.Y., we get Sexxx Dreams! Lyrically, the song is about the sexual encounters Gaga has with a woman (or possibly man) in her dreams every night. However, the song becomes a little more complex and hard to understand when you realize that Gaga is in fact singing to three different lovers in this song - the lover who she sees in her sex dreams, her current boyfriend, and her ex-boyfriend. Additionally, what's so interesting about this track is that it makes some very obvious references to the novel 1984 by George Orwell (it actually isn't the only track on the CD to reference a classic novel) and satirically compares sexual thoughts to a \\"crime.\\" As the lyrics say, \\"we're both convicted criminals of thought\\" and \\"we can't hide the evidence in our heads\\". Gaga and her dream lover will have to attend \\"the trial of this doubtful law.\\" This particular choice of words (crime, criminals, evidence, trial) further reassures this interpretation. Although many will dismiss it as just another pop song about sex, it's really quite an interesting commentary on how we perceive and even demonize sexual exploration of the human body. However, even without this analysis, the song is really great and hooks you in right away with some very hard beats and seductive vocals. Also, fair warning, the track alludes to masturbation, in case that kind of stuff bothers you. But then again, what were you expecting from a song with this title?<br /><br />5. Jewels N' Drugs (featuring T.I., Too $hort, and Twista)<br /><br />Wow! It's Gaga rapping, y'all! Not much to say about this one. I personally am not a huge fan of hip hop, but I can appreciate good rap song when I hear it. Plus, it appears that most of the general public who's listened to the album is really fond of this song. We get rap verses from T.I., Too $hort, Twista and even Gaga herself, as well as an obligatory pop versefrom Gaga. Lyrically, the meaning of the song can be summed up by its chorus, \\"Don't want your jewels, don't want your drugs, don't want your money, just want your love.\\" Not a favorite per se, but still very good. Gaga shows musically diversity and versatility here, as well as in other songs on the album, by breaking free from her usual genre and trying out something new. My favorite line, \\"I admit that my habit's expensive and you may find it quite offensive, but I won't die at the hands of another. I'm your mother, sister, your father, brother.\\"<br /><br />6. MANiCURE<br /><br />Rock n roll Gaga is back on this track! This is one of my favorite songs on the album because, not only is the chorus incredibly catchy and danceable, but Gaga's vocal delivery is just astounding here. Her voice is very powerful on this track immediately from its abrupt hits-you-in-the-face beginning, and the instruments are very rock -- this is not a pop song!! Lyrically, the song makes use a clever pun: the woman mentioned in the song wants to be get a manicure (she wants to be \\"manicured\\") but really, what Gaga is saying is that she wants to be cured from liking men (she wants to be \\"man-cured\\"). Or, at least, cured from falling in love with guys so easily. It may not be the best play on words, but it is a smart one and the way you perceive the song definitely changes once you notice the double meaning. Overall, even if you don't spot the pun, it's still an awesome track to dance to and you can just go on thinking it's really just a song about getting a manicure.<br /><br />7. Do What U Want With My Body (featuring R. Kelly)<br /><br />Gaga and R. Kelly give the haters and critics a huge middle finger with this R&B song. Despite the suggestive title, the song is actually not sexual in content once you understand the context of the statement repeated over and over in the chorus. Lyrically, this track is pretty freakin' genius. Gaga is telling the harsh and cruel critics (probably the ones who criticized her weight gain in mid 2012) that they cannot have her heart or her mind, but that they can do whatever they want to her body. She's essentially saying that as a performer, her body belongs to the public to some extent. She is a product - a brand name you see in stores - and you can \\"purchase her\\" when you buy one of her albums or go to one of her concerts. So, do what you want to her body [the vessel for her performances] because you are entitled to it and its potentially corporal vanity (the idea that female pop singers show off too much skin), its physicality, and its mortality. However, you are not allowed to touch or even close to Gaga's heart [her feelings and emotions that give her love songs meaning] or her mind [the place of origin for her creativity] because those things only belong to her and her alone, and they (the critics) do not deserve it and have not earned access to it. Honestly, that's a really great thing to write a song about. R. Kelly's softer voice surprisingly goes really well with Gaga's harder vocals and together, the duo makes this song one of the best ones on the album. I assume Gaga chose R. Kelly over other artists for this collaboration due to his scandal from a few years ago and his relation to the media. That clearly goes hand in hand with the meaning and message of the song. \\"You can't have my heart and you won't use my mind, so do what you want with my body! You won't stop my voice cause you don't own my life, so do what you want with my body!\\"<br /><br />8. ARTPOP<br /><br />The placement of this song is really crucial. There is a reason why this song isn't at the beginning or at the end of the album, but instead is located right in the middle. The song serves as a reminder that Gaga's art \\"could mean anything,\\" as the lyric states. That's basically saying to keep in mind that these songs have more than one layer of meaning to them and in order to enjoy the \\"ART\\" part of ARTPOP, you have to be aware of the multiple lyrical interpretations of the various songs. Otherwise, you just get the \\"POP\\" part of ARTPOP, which is pop music and nothing more. If you want the full package, pop music with artistic value to it, you have to start reading in between the lines. You have to realize that the song Aura does not talk about a literal burqa, but rather a metaphorical one. You have to realize that Do What U Want isn't really about doing whatever you want to Gaga's body, but instead is actually a very intelligent rant to the critics. THAT is what this song is about. Now, musically, this track is very hypnotic and mesmerizing and should absolutely be listened to with quality headphones in order to appreciate all of its beauty. The \\"laid back\\" and \\"chill\\" feel of the instrumental alone is enough to make this one of the best tracks on the CD. It kind of gives me an oldies vibe. Also, in case you don't realize this, she isn't singing to a person in this song. She is LITERALLY singing to the art and the music. My favorite line is one that really encapsulates the very essence of Gaga as an artist: \\"A hybrid can withstand these things, my heart can beat with bricks and strings, my ARTPOP could mean anything.\\" (The hybrid can refer to the Gaga-motorcycle from Born This Way - that idea that fantasy and reality can exist together, though it probably refers to art and pop united as one entity).<br /><br />9. Swine<br /><br />Swine is the perfect example of why the song \\"ARTPOP\\" is right in the middle of the tracklist. You have to remember that these songs have more than one meaning. On the surface, Swine simply seems to be about a disgusting man who is hitting on Gaga at a night club. But upon a deeper look at the lyrics, this song could very well be (and most likely is) about rape and/or other forms of sexual abuse. There is a contrast between the undoubtedly depressing lyrics that demonstrate hurt and pain (\\"I know, I know, I know, I know you want me. You're just a pig inside a human body. Squealer, squealer, squeal out, you're so disgusting!\\") with the crazy electronic beats and rhythm that purposely overshadows the meaning and even may not make allow you to notice the power of the verses and chorus. This is, by far, the most EDM track on the whole CD. It's as if Gaga is trying to cope with the trauma by making this song happy and upbeat. There is also a reference to Lord of the Flies at the end of the song (\\"paint your face and paint his face and catch the beat\\"), which makes sense since a pig head is a major plot point in that book and this song is, after all, titled Swine. If you think about how this song would sound acoustically as opposed to the electronic dance monster that it is, you will REALLY understand the meaning behind it.<br /><br />10. Donatella<br /><br />All sugar coating aside, this song is straight up about being rich, blonde, and bitchy. It's one of the most fun and poppy songs on the album and the shout out to the actual Donatella is amazing, although this song seems to be more of a satirical take on Gaga herself. A parody of Gaga from The Fame era. The song is undeniably shallow but, to me, it seems as if it's poking fun at what people assume strong and independent out-spoken women are like and the lyrics therefore should not be taken literally but still seriously.<br /><br />11. Fashion!<br /><br />The song is practically the opposite of Donatella, which is why it comes right after it. Song order matters! Gaga talk about fashion from an artistic perspective, as opposed to the way she talks about it in Donatella which is basically \\"I'm fabulous in my expensive clothing, look at me.\\" The vocals are slower and softer and the song is supposed to sound more beautiful and less of a club banger. The chorus gets stuck on your head easily, too. Be warned! Addictive chorus! Though I wouldn't necessarily call this a highlight of the album, it is definitely one of its hidden gems that grows on you the more and more you listen to it. I reallyenjoy Gaga's voice here.<br /><br />12. Mary Jane Holland<br /><br />Just like how Donatella and Fashion! are essentially grouped together and compliment each other, this song (Mary Jane Holland) and the next song on the album (Dope) are also grouped together and also serve as polar opposites of each other. Musically and sonically, Mary Jane Holland is probably one of the best songs on the CD. The beats are sick and make you just want to dance nonstop to this song. Lyrically, yes, the song is about marijuana. But it's more than just that. Though yes, at first glance the lyrics seem to imply that smoking weed recreationally can be fun, some of the other lyrics also seem to suggest that smoking pot is equivalent to making a deal with the Devil, thus illustrating the dangers of temptations. This song is the yin to the yang of Dope and has to be listened with Dope to get the full picture of what Gaga is trying to say. And by the way, my favorite line is, \\"I don't mean to boast but our troubles are the most mad-magical in Amsterdam. So if you have fear Apollo, sit on my lyre and play it like a piano man!\\" No, this song is not four minutes and twenty seconds long.<br /><br />13. Dope<br /><br />Dope is a very slow piano ballad with beautifully sad lyrics. This song contrasts Mary Jane Holland greatly and basically explores to dark side of cannabis consumption. Gaga is singing the depressing lyrics to her lover, telling him that she will find a cure for her drug addiction because she needs him more than the drug. Dope pretty much throws out the window any pro-drug message that Mary Jane Holland may have potentially conbeyed. It is the \\"low\\" to the \\"high\\" of MJH and the lyrics truly are moving and beautiful. Gaga really shows off her powerful vocals here as well as her songwriting talents (show this track to anyone who dares to say that Gaga cannot sing!) My favorite line is, \\"My heart might break without you, might not awake without you. Been hurting low from living high for so long. I'm sorry that I love you, sing with me Bell Bottom Blues. I'll keep on searching for an answer cause I need you more than dope.\\" The piano on this track is also really wonderful. This is, hands down, one of the most emotional tracks on the CD and you can real FEEL that raw emotion in her voice.<br /><br />14. Gypsy<br /><br />Gypsy is another one of the slower songs on the album, though nowhere near as slow as Dope. Once again, this song shows off Gaga's vocals and songwriting skills moreso than the other songs on the album. Gypsy probably has the best lyrics of any track on the whole CD and the energetic beat can be compared to that of The Edge Of Glory from Born This Way. Lyrically, the song is about two lovers who can't be together because one travels the world. I don't like to say that songs are flawless because that's just my opinion and therefore subjective, but let's be real, this song really is flawless! This is one of the best songs Lady Gaga has written in her entire professional career. I dare say this it is my absolute favorite song in all of ARTPOP. I love the imagery Gaga evokes about chasing the sunset and driving away in your car and also, I love the line, \\"And then he asked me, he said, 'Baby, why do we love each other?' I said, 'Honey it's simple, it's the way that you love and treat your mother.'\\" I'll admit that that line made me get a little teary and smile like a dork. Another great line: \\"So I just packed my baggage and, said good bye to family and friends, and took the road to nowhere on my own... Like Dorothy on the yellow brick, hope my ruby shoes get us there quick, cause I left everyone I love at home...\\" Gypsy is a very memorable track.<br /><br />15. Applause<br /><br />What a great way to end the CD...with a big round of applause! This song reminds us that Gaga does not live for the fame and the money, but rather for the applause of her fans. If you really pay attention to the lyrics, the song is pretty much a huge thank you to the fans as well as an ode to the theatre and the art of performing. The David Bowie-esque vocals in the verses and the catchy chorus makes this track one of the highlights of the album, even if we had  already heard it before. My favorite thing about this song (other than the shout out to Jeff Koons in the second verse) is that Gaga reminds us that she is an ARTIST, not a celebrity, and that her work always has meaning. It isn't just fun bubblegum pop music to dance to. \\"Pop culture was in art, now art's in pop culture in me.\\" I actually did a more extensive review of this song when it came out, you can read it here:[[ASIN:B00EJYGQFG Applause]]<br /><br />So, why did I take my time to analyze each and every one of the songs? Because that's the whole point about Lady Gaga. It's pop music with meaning. It always has been that way with her. The lyrics are intelligent and well written and if you don't appreciate that, then you're missing 80% of what makes Gaga so different from the rest of her female contemporaries. She spent 2+ years making this record, so you can bet it's not just a bunch of random pop songs with simplistic lyrics thrown together. Sure, people will claim that it is. People will say it's style over substance, that it's pretentious, that its just like her past work and nothing new, and that I'm reading too much into it because some people can't fathom that pop music can be deep too (and also because hating on Lady Gaga has become a rather popular think to do). These are probably the people who don't WANT to look at the art behind the work and then complain that there is no art, and who most likely prefer the mainstream pop of this generation that has unfortunately given pop music a bad name in the last couple of years. Despite the length of my review and the analysis I present, I can bet this going to receive a lot of thumbs down by those very people.<br /><br />But let's not forget that this woman hasn't been praised by The Rolling Stones, KISS, Paul McCartney, Sting, Tony Bennett, Bruce Springsteen, Cyndi Lauper, Blondie, and Brian May (from Queen) for nothing. They know about good music and they like Gaga. If that doesn't validate Gaga as an artist, then I don't know what does. And given that the title of this record is ARTPOP, you can bet that the artistic references found in these songs are very much on purpose and should therefore be noted and not taken for granted. It's not just me over-analyzing pop music; the title of the work is literally ARTPOP for crying out loud!<br /><br />Lady Gaga is already making history with this album, and that is no exaggeration. The marble sculpture of Gaga shown on the cover of the album was done by none other than the legendary Jeff Koons, who also famously sculpted Michael Jackson and Bubbles back in 1988. Additionally, at the album release party Gaga threw in New York on the day that ARTPOP came out, she debuted the world's first ever flying dress (yes, it ACTUALLY flies!) that she had TechHaus - a branch of Haus Of Gaga - specifically build for her for ARTPOP performances and her upcoming world tour. She's also performing a track from ARTPOP in space in 2015, and will be the first artist ever to sing in outer space.<br /><br />In conclusion, you can bet that this album is going to get hate - in fact, count on it - but ARTPOP is an amazing pop album with amazing beats and lyrical content. Some will like it because it's a great party album you might hear in a club. Others will like it for the metaphorical lyrics, metaphors, and art references. All in all, Gaga does not disappoint and this album will go down in pop music history.<br /><br />Also, Gaga has developed a free app for smart phones where bonus tracks will be released, the first of them being a song called TEA.<br /><br />Favorite songs: Gypsy, Aura, Dope, Venus, G.U.Y., Swine, ARTPOP, Applause, Mary Jane Holland, Sexxx Dreams, MANiCURE, Do What U Want.<br /><br />Lyrics: A+ (Gaga's poet shines through hersongwriting)<br /><br />Production: A+ (Zedd, Madeon, and DJWS did an amazing job)<br /><br />Cover: good representation of the themes explored throughout the body of work. POP is on the front of ART while still merging with it. Renaissance art (Botticelli's Birth of Venus), contemporary art (Jeff Koons' Gazing Ball), Baroque art (Bernini's Apollo and Daphne), performance art (Lady Gaga) are all present on the cover.<br /><br />Booklet: photo shoot of Gaga posing for Jeff Koons for the cover.<br /><br />Warnings: explicit lyrics, adult themes, nudity in the booklet<br /><br />If you enjoy ARTPOP, I recommend giving Gaga's past albums a listen (especially Born This Way) as well as her upcoming jazz album with Mr. Tony Bennett, due in stores on New Year's Day.le lyrical interpretations of the various songs. Otherwise, you just get the \\"POP\\" part of ARTPOP, which is pop music and nothing more. If you want the full package, pop music with artistic value to it, you have to start reading in between the lines. You have to realize that the song Aura does not talk about a literal burqa, but rather a metaphorical one. You have to realize that Do What U Want isn't really about doing whatever you want to Gaga's body, but instead is actually a very intelligent rant to the critics. THAT is what this song is about. Now, musically, this track is very hypnotic and mesmerizing and should absolutely be listened to with quality headphones in order to appreciate all of its beauty. The \\"laid back\\" and \\"chill\\" feel of the instrumental alone is enough to make this one of the best tracks on the CD. It kind of gives me an oldies vibe. Also, in case you don't realize this, she isn't singing to a person in this song. She is LITERALLY singing to the art and the music. My favorite line is one that really encapsulates the very essence of Gaga as an artist: \\"A hybrid can withstand these things, my heart can beat with bricks and strings, my ARTPOP could mean anything.\\" (The hybrid can refer to the Gaga-motorcycle from Born This Way - that idea that fantasy and reality can exist together, though it probably refers to art and pop united as one entity).<br /><br />9. Swine<br /><br />Swine is the perfect example of why the song \\"ARTPOP\\" is right in the middle of the tracklist. You have to remember that these songs have more than one meaning. On the surface, Swine simply seems to be about a disgusting man who is hitting on Gaga at a night club. But upon a deeper look at the lyrics, this song could very well be (and most likely is) about rape and/or other forms of sexual abuse. There is a contrast between the undoubtedly depressing lyrics that demonstrate hurt and pain (\\"I know, I know, I know, I know you want me. You're just a pig inside a human body. Squealer, squealer, squeal out, you're so disgusting!\\") with the crazy electronic beats and rhythm that purposely overshadows the meaning and even may not make allow you to notice the power of the verses and chorus. This is, by far, the most EDM track on the whole CD. It's as if Gaga is trying to cope with the trauma by making this song happy and upbeat. There is also a reference to Lord of the Flies at the end of the song (\\"paint your face and paint his face and catch the beat\\"), which makes sense since a pig head is a major plot point in that book and this song is, after all, titled Swine. If you think about how this song would sound acoustically as opposed to the electronic dance monster that it is, you will REALLY understand the meaning behind it.<br /><br />10. Donatella<br /><br />All sugar coating aside, this song is straight up about being rich, blonde, and bitchy. It's one of the most fun and poppy songs on the album and the shout out to the actual Donatella is amazing, although this song seems to be more of a satirical take on Gaga herself. A parody of Gaga from The Fame era. The song is undeniably shallow but, to me, it seems as if it's poking fun at what people assume strong and independent out-spoken women are like and the lyrics therefore should not be taken literally but still seriously.<br /><br />11. B00CSYRHG6|4.0|Based on a serial graphic comic from the 1980s, \\"From Up on Poppy Hill\\" is a sweet and gentle Japanese anime drama set in 1963, right on the eve of that nation's hosting of the Tokyo Olympics.<br /><br />Voiced by Sarah Bolger in the English version, Umi is a high school girl whose mother is studying in America and whose father has apparently died in the Korean War. She currently lives in a boarding house run by her grandmother where she cooks the meals for the residents and her two younger sisters. Umi also raises flags everyday in the hope that her father, whose body has never been found, will find his way to her. Umi has also fallen for a cute boy, the publisher of the school newspaper, and, through him, she becomes instrumental in helping to save a clubhouse the philosophy geeks use for their meetings and which has been threatened with demolition by the higher-ups who are more interested in modernizing war-ravaged Japan than in holding onto relics of the past.<br /><br />Directed by Goro Miyazaki, \\"Poppy Hill\\" is an old-fashioned, no-fuss movie that deliberately avoids the CGI effects and hectic style of most modern animated movies. The use of cell-drawn animation yields an uncluttered palette that nicely matches the storyline. The characters' movements are fairly stiff and the facial expressions virtually nonexistent, but the background has a lovely watercolor appearance that captures the visual simplicity of an earlier era.<br /><br />The screenplay by  Hayao Miyazaki and Keiko Niwa lacks focus at times, but that actually adds to the movie's charm since we don't feel as if we're watching an overly contrived narrative designed to make points. As such, it's a movie that youngsters in particular will find reflective of their own concerns and lives, regardless of nationality.

B00EW9GQR6|2.0|I'm guessing this review will be voted down by rabid fans.<br /><br />What's left to say about Lady GaGa that hasn't already been said about her? It's trendy to hate on this woman, and I should know. But is she deserving of all the controversy? Not anymore, no. After exploding on the scene with a bombshell of an album, The Fame, and then its supplement The Fame Monster, it seemed that Lady GaGa could do absolutely no wrong. But then Born This Way happened. And it polarized every listener of pop music between \\"I hate this woman\\" and \\"I love this woman.\\" I fell into the first category. Madonna comparisons aside, the album was a mess of electronic beats that literally hurt to listen to. There were some nice production tricks here and there, but the monotonity and pretense surrounding the project overshadowed any of its positive aspects. It was a misguided attempt at ego inflation that ended up offending, well, just about everyone. Except the people she meant to offend (the Catholic church, I think). After about a year of bad press and critical scrutiny, despite a successful display of singles, Lady GaGa just dropped off the face of the Earth as best she could. She had surgery, reportedly concerning her hip, cancelled a portion of her Born This Way Ball Tour, and began work on her next incarnation. As much as I dislike Lady GaGa, I do try to give her the benefit of the doubt and give her the chance to redeem herself. Maybe she'll pull out another unpretentious song like Just Dance or Starstruck. My problem with Lady GaGa is that she began to sing about things she really knew nothing about. She's a socialite-brat-art-school-drama-kid who liked to party and dress in funny costumes. If nothing else, at least The Fame was believable and honest.<br /><br />And it seems that Lady GaGa has partially returned back to what made the world fall in love with her. ARTPOP, her forth abum (in my opinion The Fame Monster is its own separate entity), is a collection of odd pop songs that on the surface is just a party record. But there's a lot more here. It's far less artistic than perhaps she wants us to believe, but at least it's more genuine than Born This Way was. The biggest issue with ARTPOP is that just about every song is hookless, forgettable and remarkably unimaginative. Her hype has certainly taken center stage, her fashion sense second priority, and her music is somewhere on the middle the list just above wiping her butt. ARTPOP has rapidly devolved GaGa back into the party girl we all knew she was, but it kept all of the same pretense of Born This Way. And this is evidenced best on the album's opener, the woefully embarrassing Aura, which already caused quite the splash for its misappropriation of Islamic culture. Not really surprised. It seems nothing is all that sacred when it comes to whatever will keep Lady GaGa's names in the paper.<br /><br />But is it all bad? No. Not really. There are some delicious beats here, far better than those on her previous record, and the production is slicker. Also, GaGa's voice has drastically improved. She's sounds far moe operatic than she did on The Fame or Born This Way, and I find her a lot easier to listen to. The problem with ARTPOP really is that the material is weak and bland, something I wouldn't necessarily expect from her. This album is mostly stuff I might expect from Britney Spears, Ke$ha, or Katy Perry. Say what you want about Lady GaGa, and trust me I have said everything already, at least stuff like Bad Romance is distinctly GaGa and could be sung by nobody but her. ARTPOP just lacks the personality that made the woman memorable. Stuff like Fashion! and Sexx Dreams are not bad tracks. I wouldn't be annoyed if I heard them while shopping in a store or if they came on the radio; but I can't believe they even made the cut for what has been lauded as GaGa's return to form. They sound like watered down Fame songs.<br /><br />The leading single, Applause, was the first sign that GaGa might serioulsy be on the decline. Of course this album will not be unsuccessful-- only unsuccesful when compared to her previous efforts-- but it is a sign of things to come. The general public seems  disinterested at this point as she is now longer polarizing people but rather she's just boring them to tears. Songs like the worthless and unnecessarily maudlin Dope are not really going to have people running to jump back on the GaGa wagon. I guess I just don't get it. Maybe I'm not cool enough, but I just can't understand why all of a sudden GaGa has gone from making waves to just barely catching them. Gypsy has a lovely melody, some of her best lyrics (until it culminates in that awful ending bridge), and is one of her better attempts at balladry, but the production sounds like something Ne-Yo and Pitbull might come up with. It just feels odd. GaGa might be slipping a little bit. I feel like she's lost her way. There's something in the music of ARTPOP that feels humbled over Born This Way, but all the hype surrounding kind of pollutes the idea that she's gotten over herself.<br /><br />At the end of the day, Applause is probably the most GaGa song on this record, and if you didn't like that song, you likely won't like the rest of this album too much either. That said, it is worthy to say that Mary Jane Holland might the overall album standout. Despite being a trashy ode to what Lady GaGa calls a marijuana \\"addiction\\" (get real, GaGa), it has just enough pop smarts to worm its way into your head the same way Just Dance did.<br /><br />Listen to: Gypsy, Mary Jane Holland

B00ECL7ZJ2|5.0|I discovered this band on one of those rare occasions when MTV actually played a video. \\"Don't Save Me\\" demonstrated brash swagger against a driving backbeat, and the video emphasized the Haim sisters' playful chutzpah. (YouTube  it; you'll thank me.) I'm pleased to say, the entire album maintains that lead single's momentum. For a staunch anti-modernist like me, it's strange to say, but this band makes me happy to be alive right now.<br /><br />The Haim sisters utilize elements I recognize from the synthpop that dominated radio during my grade school days. Hints of The Human League, Til Tuesday, and The Thompson Twins permeate their sound. But Haim isn't interested in mere imitation; they cherry-pick what suits their artistic vision and discard the rest. Importantly, their instruments, not the digital effects, dominate their sound. They're a musicians' band, not a studio phenomenon.<br /><br />Tracks like \\"The Wire\\" and \\"Honey & I\\" symbolize their dominant themes, particularly a woman's desire to captain her own romantic life. Not for them the girlish pleadings of Top-40 acts like Britney (though they don't flinch from broken-heart confessionals like \\"If I Could Change Your Mind\\"). Haim makes music for grown-ups, with real adult aspirations for mature control in meaningful relationships. No wonder mothers and daughters embrace them with equal fervor.<br /><br />In a music industry dominated by shrinking violets or chintzy Katy Perry-ish temptresses, the Haim sisters really impress me with their mature, thoughtful, yet playfully danceable music. Their sound reflects their breezy Los Angeles roots, the same milieu that birthed the Eagles' later albums. But they'll also feel familiar to those of us weaned on the Second British Invasion. The sober adult themes and sonically complex arrangements create music I just enjoy hearing.

B008JFUPK8|5.0|There have been numerous opinions about positive and negative points dealing with this film. No movie will ever be perfect and please everyone but I have to applaud Zack Schneider for giving us a new vision of Superman never seen on screen before. When 'Superman Returns' came out in 2006 most fanboys were screaming about having no action in the film. \\"Superman didn't even throw a punch\\" was a common critique. Well, WB heard their complaints and made a 180 degree turnaround. As far as I'm concerned, they went from one extreme to the other. I've described this film to others as a rollercoaster ride that rarely stops. It's shocking how much is thrown at you during the course of this story.<br />You will not see a Clark Kent with perfect parents who bake apple pies and have the perfect answers for any questions Clark has. You will not see a completely happy childhood where little Clark has no real cares and worries until his father dies. You will not find a Superman who has all of the answers of exactly what he needs to do to solve a problem. This is a movie where Clark is uncertain who he is and doesn't necessarily want to have his powers and abilities that set him apart from everyone else causing him to be a target by others. He learns how to control his anger with people he would be able to turn into a pretzel if he wanted to. He does not know how to deal with another kryptonian named Zod who wishes to rule planet earth. He just knows he needs to stop him from this alien invasion.<br />There are a few scenes that I believe were inspired partially from the Avengers. When Superman is handcuffed and marched into custody it is almost exactly the kind of shot used when Loki was marched to his cell in the Avengers. Near the end of the film there is an invasion that also takes me back to be Avengers inspired. Is that bad? I would say no. Zack Schneider had a tremendous undertaking to take a hero who was losing interest to Batman and give him a huge comeback while also setting up a DC universe of films at the same time.<br />There were big changes made to Superman's origin story. There are changes in how his father dies. His fortress of solitude is very different than what you imagine in any other Superman film before it. But none of these things take away from the identity of the character of Superman. Only people like me who grew up with the Reeve version may try to compare films like this.<br />Of course, there is an extremely controversial ending. If you don't know what I mean, this is a SPOILER ALERT.... Superman makes the ultimate life or death decision to either allow Zod to continue his mission of death to all humans or stop him. In one pivotal scene he makes the quick decision to break Zod's neck rather than allow him to do any more killing and destruction. Some people were screaming how Superman doesn't kill. They need to realize that Superman has killed before. For goodness sakes, he fought and killed Doomsday in the comics. In Superman II he allows the three Kryptonian villains to fall to their death. In Schneider's world Superman doesn't have the hard and fast rule that you NEVER take a life. He made this decision based on the basis of a killer who cannot be killed. And now he will live with it for the rest of his life. For this Superman, it probably is the origin of the no-kill rule. It's going to be interesting to find out how they deal with this in the next installment.<br />I loved the casting. Russell Crow is a wonderful Jor El. There are also ties to other Superman shows. Diane Lane was in \\"Hollywoodland\\" where she played the girlfriend of George Reeves, the actor who portrayed Superman in the 1950s. By the way, I also was very excited to find out Ben Affleck will be Batman in the sequel because he played George Reeves in the previously mentioned movie and donned a Superman costume. Lois Lane Amy Adams was in the first season of Smallville. For me it was just fun to watch these characters who had a Superman connection previously.<br />Was it a perfect film? No. Name one film that is. But it does do justice to the world's first Superhero and tried to find a balance between the darkness of Batman and the opposite brightness of Superman. This movie is not a bright one like the previous films. It is shot in a grittier fashion. For those seeking a Superman film with bright scenes and beautiful colors, you won't find it here. Go back to the Reeve films. But Superman is finally given a story that many fans have been waiting a very long time to see. I think it's a very well done film and I hope you do too. Superman flies high and seems to relate to what happens in today's world. I enjoyed it and am looking forward to the sequel in 2015.n previously.<br />Was it a perfect film? B00DYQLEZM|4.0|I was not very sure if I really wanted this box set or not. I did some research, mainly, what exactly was included here. I already had some of the CDs, so to buy a box set with stuff I already had was not something I was very happy to do. However, the Amazon price was very attractive, so I decided to go ahead and buy it. I paid $100.49 for this, so that meant a couples of bucks for each CD, which is a real bargain.<br /><br />I am not going to spend time discussing here whether the Berliner Philharmoniker is one of the best orchestras in the world or not. It is in my Top 5 list. This is a very personal choice, so this may or may not help you decide to go ahead and get this box set. Unless you have most of these releases already.<br /><br />This may be obvious, but the core of the box set is Herbert von Karajan. A total of 15 CDs are his signature. Among them, Beethoven's 9th (1963), Mahler's 5th (1973, his first Mahler ever, and my favorite one), and Schostakovitch's 10th (1982, magisterial!) are among the best of this box set. You can also find his Bizet's Carmen (highlights), Wagner's Parsifal (highlights), and Mozart Great Mass. The Schoenberg is included, but beware, this does not match the Legendary Recordings editions. There, his Verkl&auml;rte is paired with Pelleas. Here, the original CD is presented, which includes Verkl&auml;rte Nacht, Variations for Orchestra (a must IMHO), and Webern's Passacaglia.<br /><br />After Karajan, you have B&ouml;hm and Abbado. My favorite Abbado here is Prokofiev and Ravel Piano Concertos with Martha Argerich. I have most of Argerich's recordings on EMI and DG, so again, nothing new, but for those who don't know her, or don't have this particular recording, this is perhaps the best interpretations you can listen to. Abbado has done a lot of Mahler, and his 4th (2005) is included here. Also Beethoven's 7th and 8th are included (I believe these are the same ones he published on DVD, which I also own). B&ouml;hm is represented with 3 CDs. Beethoven's Missa Solemnis, Mozart's 40th and 41st, and highlights of his Zauberfl&ouml;te.<br /><br />The rest of the box is very mixed, with recordings as old as Nikisch Beethoven's 5th from 1913 (horrible sound, of course), or Furtw&auml;ngler Beethoven 5th (1926, more horrible sound), to Rattle's Dvorak's biblical Songs (2012, so new, the CD does not even have art cover for it!). In between, Beethoven's Piano Concerto NO. 5 (two: Kempff and Pollini), Beethoven's 9th (two: Karajan and Fricsay), Dvorak's Cello concerto (twice -?!-, but the Rostropovich in my opinion is absolutely essential), Dvorak's 9th (two: Fricsay and, thank you! Kubelik!!!), Bernstein's Mahler No. 9 (Karajan's 9th version of Mahler also included), Boulez's Ravel Bolero, etc. I'd suggest you go to DG's website to read the contents before you purchase, to make sure you like what's included, or to double check your collection and see if you already have most of this.<br /><br />The box is nicely packaged, and the CDs are contained in cardboard sleeves. Most of them come with the original art work, except for CD #50, and the first 10. A libretto is included, but unlike other reviewers have noted, I don't find it to be exemplary at all. It's 96 pages long, and it comes with `A word of greeting from the Berliner Philharmoniker,' `The edition of the century.' `The Berliner Philharmoniker and DG: A creative partnership of 100 years.' These texts are in English, German, and Japanese. The booklet explains the way this selection was done, which was by asking patrons of the orchestra to decide which releases to include. I find this to be a very original way to approach a box set like this, although the results will not be satisfactory for some. The booklet is completed with the track lists of all CDs, and a final index by composers (39 composers in total!).<br /><br />Pros: Price. It includes some of the greatest classical recordings of all time (although you probably have them...).<br />Cons:The few operas represented are only highlights. Although understandable in a box set, it would have been better just to not include them at all, or include two full operas (I'd say Wagner's Parsifal by Karajan, and Mozart's Magic Flute by B&ouml;hm). A lot of repeated works. You may have many of this releases already.<br /><br />In summary, this is a great collection of excellent classical music recordings by one of the greatest orchestras of all time. This box set will be out of the market soon, and therefore, hard or impossible to find. If you like the Berliner Philharmoniker, Karajan, or just classical music in general, get it while it is available, especially at the $100 price. You may want to pass it if you have most of the albums here, though. Not essential, but highly recommendable. Thus, 4 stars. Thank you for reading.The few operas represented are only highlights. Although understandable in a box set, it would have been better just to not include them at all, or include two full operas (I'd say Wagner's Parsifal by Karajan, and Mozart's Magic Flute by B&ouml;hm). A lot of repeated works. You may have many of this releases already.<br /><br />In summary, this is a great collection of excellent classical music recordings by one of the greatest orchestras of all time. This box set will be out of the market soon, and therefore, hard or impossible to find. If you like the Berliner Philharmoniker, Karajan, or just classical music in general, get it while it is available, especially at the $100 price. You may want to pass it if you have most of the albums here, though. Not essential, but highly recommendable. Thus, 4 stars. Thank you for reading.
